<td>55,000
</td></tr></tbody></table></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Card_products">Card products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Card products" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<p>As of 31 December 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the company had 114.4 million cards in force, including 54.7<span class="nowrap"> </span>million cards in force in the United States, each with an average annual spending of $19,972.<sup id="cite_ref-10-K_2019_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10-K_2019-4">[4]</a></sup> These include consumer, small business and corporate cards issued by American Express themselves and cards issued by its Global Service Network partners that run on its network (such as Commonwealth Bank, Westpac and NAB in Australia and Lloyds Bank and Barclays Bank in the UK). On March 1, 2017, Australia's fourth largest bank ANZ announced that it was no longer issuing American Express cards, with the support phased out entirely by August 5, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p><p>American Express is the fourth largest general-purpose card network on a global basis based on purchase volume, behind China UnionPay, Visa and MasterCard.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> It is the 4th largest card network in the world, based on the number of cards it has in circulation.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p><p>American Express is one of the partner banks to both <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> and <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a>'s mobile wallet systems (<a href="/wiki/Google_Pay" title="Google Pay">Google Pay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Apple_Pay" title="Apple Pay">Apple Pay</a>, respectively) meaning that cardholders can use their American Express-issued cards to pay at establishments where <a href="/wiki/Near_field_communication" class="mw-redirect" title="Near field communication">NFC</a> payments are accepted. American Express offers various <a href="/wiki/Contactless_smart_card" title="Contactless smart card">contactless credit cards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Consumer_cards">Consumer cards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Consumer cards" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HK_West_Kln_Waterfront_Promenade_Hong_Kong_Wine_%26_Dine_Festival_Nov-2012_booths_American_Express_sponsor_view_ICC.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/HK_West_Kln_Waterfront_Promenade_Hong_Kong_Wine_%26_Dine_Festival_Nov-2012_booths_American_Express_sponsor_view_ICC.JPG/260px-HK_West_Kln_Waterfront_Promenade_Hong_Kong_Wine_%26_Dine_Festival_Nov-2012_booths_American_Express_sponsor_view_ICC.JPG" decoding="async" width="260" height="194" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1936"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 260px;height: 194px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/HK_West_Kln_Waterfront_Promenade_Hong_Kong_Wine_%26_Dine_Festival_Nov-2012_booths_American_Express_sponsor_view_ICC.JPG/260px-HK_West_Kln_Waterfront_Promenade_Hong_Kong_Wine_%26_Dine_Festival_Nov-2012_booths_American_Express_sponsor_view_ICC.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="260" data-height="194" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HK_West_Kln_Waterfront_Promenade_Hong_Kong_Wine_%26_Dine_Festival_Nov-2012_booths_American_Express_sponsor_view_ICC.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An advertisement for the American Express Platinum Credit Card in Hong Kong</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Centurion_Card" title="Centurion Card">Centurion Card</a> and <a href="/wiki/Accolades_Card" title="Accolades Card">Accolades Card</a></div>
<p>American Express is best known for its Green, Gold, and Platinum charge cards.  The Gold Card has recently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (September 2019)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> been converted to a credit card for UK residents but remains a charge card in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p><p>In 1958, American Express issued its first <a href="/wiki/Charge_card" title="Charge card">charge card</a>, which required payment at the end of every month.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> In 1966, the company issued its first gold card, in an effort to cater to the upper echelon of business travel.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Its platinum card debuted in 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p><p>In 1999, American Express introduced the <a href="/wiki/Centurion_Card" title="Centurion Card">Centurion Card</a>, often referred to as the "black card," which caters to an even more affluent customer segment. The card was initially available only to select users of the Platinum card. The annual fee for the card in the United States is $5,000 (up from $1,000 at introduction) with an additional one-time initiation fee of $10,000. American Express created the card line amid rumors and <a href="/wiki/Urban_legend" title="Urban legend">urban legends</a> in the 1980s that it produced an ultra-exclusive black card for elite users who could purchase anything with it.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p><p>American Express cards issued in the United States range in cost between no annual fee (for Blue and many other consumer and business cards) and a $550 annual fee (for the Platinum card).<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Annual fees for the Green card start at $150, while Gold card annual fees start at $250.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p><p>American Express has several co-branded credit cards, with most falling into one of three categories:
</p>
<ul><li>Airlines: <a href="/wiki/Aerolineas_Argentinas" class="mw-redirect" title="Aerolineas Argentinas">Aerolineas Argentinas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aerom%C3%A9xico" title="Aeroméxico">Aeroméxico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_Canada" title="Air Canada">Air Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alitalia" title="Alitalia">Alitalia</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cathay_Pacific" title="Cathay Pacific">Cathay Pacific</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Icelandair" title="Icelandair">Icelandair</a>, <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qantas" title="Qantas">Qantas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">Scandinavian Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/SriLankan_Airlines" title="SriLankan Airlines">SriLankan Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thai_Airways" title="Thai Airways">Thai Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">Virgin Atlantic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Australia" title="Virgin Australia">Virgin Australia</a>, among others.</li>
<li>Hotels: <a href="/wiki/Best_Western" title="Best Western">Best Western</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hilton_Hotels" class="mw-redirect" title="Hilton Hotels">Hilton Hotels</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marriott_International" title="Marriott International">Marriott International</a></li>
<li>Retailers: <a href="/wiki/David_Jones_Limited" title="David Jones Limited">David Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holt_Renfrew" title="Holt Renfrew">Holt Renfrew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harrods" title="Harrods">Harrods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy's">Macy's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bloomingdales" class="mw-redirect" title="Bloomingdales">Bloomingdales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lowe%27s" title="Lowe's">Lowe's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes_Benz" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercedes Benz">Mercedes Benz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dillard%27s" title="Dillard's">Dillard's</a> and others.</li></ul><p>A credit card aimed at young adults is called <i>Blue</i>, which has no annual fee and a <a href="/wiki/Loyalty_program" title="Loyalty program">loyalty program</a>. A television media campaign for Blue adopted the 1979 UK <a href="/wiki/Synthpop" class="mw-redirect" title="Synthpop">Synthpop</a> hit "<a href="/wiki/Cars_(song)" title="Cars (song)">Cars</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Gary_Numan" title="Gary Numan">Gary Numan</a> as its <a href="/wiki/Theme_music" title="Theme music">theme music</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Cashback_reward_program" title="Cashback reward program">cashback reward program</a> version, "Blue Cash", quickly followed. American Express also targeted young adults with City Reward Cards that earn INSIDE Rewards points to eat, drink, and play at New York, Chicago and LA hot spots. American Express began phasing out the INSIDE cards in mid-2008, with no new applications being taken as of July 2008.
</p><p>In 2005, American Express introduced Clear, advertised as the first credit card with no fees of any kind.  Other cards introduced in 2005, included "The Knot" and "The Nest" Credit Cards from American Express, co-branded cards developed with the wedding planning website theknot.com.
</p><p>In 2006, the UK division of American Express joined the <a href="/wiki/Product_Red" title="Product Red">Product Red</a> coalition and issued a Red Card, donating with each purchase through <a href="/wiki/The_Global_Fund_to_Fight_AIDS,_Tuberculosis_and_Malaria" title="The Global Fund to Fight AIDS, Tuberculosis and Malaria">The Global Fund to Fight AIDS, Tuberculosis and Malaria</a> to help African women and children suffering from HIV/AIDS, malaria, and other diseases.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p><p>In 2009, American Express introduced the ZYNC charge card. White in color, this card was created for people aged 20–40.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The Zync charge card has since been discontinued with the exception of current cardholders who are <a href="/wiki/Grandfathered" class="mw-redirect" title="Grandfathered">grandfathered</a> into the ZYNC.
</p><p>In late 2012, American Express and <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a> announced the launch of Bluebird, a <a href="/wiki/Prepaid_debit_card" class="mw-redirect" title="Prepaid debit card">prepaid debit card</a> similar to that of <a href="/wiki/Green_Dot_Corporation" title="Green Dot Corporation">Green Dot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Bluebird is being touted as having some of the benefits of traditional American Express cards, such as <a href="/wiki/Roadside_assistance" title="Roadside assistance">roadside assistance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Identity_theft" title="Identity theft">identity theft</a> protection. The card can also be used as a substitute to a traditional <a href="/wiki/Transactional_account" class="mw-redirect" title="Transactional account">checking account</a>. Unlike other such cards, Bluebird is <a href="/wiki/Federal_Deposit_Insurance_Corporation" title="Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation">FDIC</a>-insured.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>  Bluebird accounts have standard FDIC deposit insurance and check writing capabilities, and customers can now<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2019)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> have Social Security payments, military pay, Tax Return, paycheck and other government benefits deposited directly into their accounts.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Card_acceptance_outside_the_United_States">Card acceptance outside the United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Card acceptance outside the United States" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>American Express credit cards are noted by travel guides, including <a href="/wiki/Rough_Guides" title="Rough Guides">Rough Guides</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lonely_Planet" title="Lonely Planet">Lonely Planet</a>, as being less commonly accepted in Europe than Visa or Mastercard.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> In an interview with an American Express spokesman in 2010, about card acceptance in the UK, the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mail" title="Daily Mail">Daily Mail</a>'</i>s financial website, <i>This is Money</i>, noted that "The list of places that are taking American Express appears to be growing, rather than slowing, but it seems to be a little hit-and-miss. It's not a good feeling to enter a shop, not knowing whether or not they accept the card."<sup id="cite_ref-thisismoney_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thisismoney-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Card_design">Card design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Card design" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The company logo, a gladiator or centurion, appears at the center of the iconic Zync, Cobalt, Green, Gold, Platinum, and Centurion cards. The figure and his pose evoke <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a>. These cards also feature intricate border and background designs that read "American Express." The designs on these cards, especially the Green card, bear resemblance to those on United States <a href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve_Notes" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Reserve Notes">Federal Reserve Notes</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="ExpressPay">ExpressPay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: ExpressPay" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:EMVCoContactlessIndicator.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="EMVCoContactlessIndicator.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/EMVCoContactlessIndicator.svg/75px-EMVCoContactlessIndicator.svg.png" decoding="async" width="75" height="91" data-file-width="46" data-file-height="56"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 75px;height: 91px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/EMVCoContactlessIndicator.svg/75px-EMVCoContactlessIndicator.svg.png" data-alt="EMVCoContactlessIndicator.svg" data-width="75" data-height="91" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/EMVCoContactlessIndicator.svg/113px-EMVCoContactlessIndicator.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/EMVCoContactlessIndicator.svg/150px-EMVCoContactlessIndicator.svg.png 2x"> </span></a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Americanexpressplatinumemvcontactless.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a7/Americanexpressplatinumemvcontactless.jpg/220px-Americanexpressplatinumemvcontactless.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="365" data-file-height="272"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 164px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a7/Americanexpressplatinumemvcontactless.jpg/220px-Americanexpressplatinumemvcontactless.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="164" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Americanexpressplatinumemvcontactless.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Platinum American Express Charge Card issued in the UK that is contactless-enabled</div></div></div>
<p>In 2005, American Express introduced ExpressPay, similar to Mastercard <a href="/wiki/Mastercard#Mastercard_Contactless" title="Mastercard">Contactless</a> and Visa <a href="/wiki/PayWave" class="mw-redirect" title="PayWave">payWave</a>, all of which use the symbol appearing on the right. It is a <a href="/wiki/Contactless_payment" title="Contactless payment">contactless payment</a> system based on wireless <a href="/wiki/RFID" class="mw-redirect" title="RFID">RFID</a>, where transactions are completed by holding the credit card near a receiver at which point the debt is immediately added to the account. All three contactless systems use the same logo. The card is not swiped or inserted into a smart card reader and no PIN is entered.
</p><p>Many merchants, in the U.S. and globally, offer American Express contactless payment, including <a href="/wiki/Meijer" title="Meijer">Meijer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walgreens" title="Walgreens">Walgreens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Best_Buy" title="Best Buy">Best Buy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Chevron Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Starbucks" title="Starbucks">Starbucks</a>, and <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Express_OPEN">American Express OPEN</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: American Express OPEN" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>American Express OPEN, the small-business branch of American Express, offers various types of charge cards for small businesses to manage their expenses.
</p><p>In late 2007, the company announced the new Plum Card as the latest addition to their card line for <a href="/wiki/Small_business" title="Small business">small business</a> owners.<sup id="cite_ref-American-Express-Oct-2007-8-K_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American-Express-Oct-2007-8-K-65">[65]</a></sup> The card provides a 1.5% early pay discount or up to two months to defer payment on purchases. The 1.5% discount is available for billing periods where the cardmember spends at least $5,000. The first 10,000 cards were issued to members on December 16, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p><p>In 2008, American Express closed all Business Line of Credit accounts. This decision was reached in tandem with the Federal Reserve's approval of American Express's request to become a <a href="/wiki/Commercial_bank" title="Commercial bank">commercial bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p><p>As of July 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, American Express has several credit cards designed for small business. These include SimplyCash Plus Business Credit Card. Cash back earned is automatically credited to the cardholder's statement and other benefits are included.  Other cards include the Business Platinum Card from American Express OPEN, the Business Gold Rewards Card from American Express OPEN, the Blue for Business Credit Card from American Express, Business Green Rewards Card from American Express OPEN, the Business Green Rewards Card from American Express OPEN and the Plum Card from American Express OPEN.  These cards have return protection, year-end summaries and other tools to help with the business accounting and control.<sup id="cite_ref-Daniel_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daniel-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_cards_and_services">Commercial cards and services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Commercial cards and services" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2008, American Express acquired the Corporate Payment Services business of GE, which primarily focused on providing Purchasing Card solutions for large global clients.<sup id="cite_ref-American-Express-Mar-2008-8-K_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American-Express-Mar-2008-8-K-69">[69]</a></sup> As part of the $1b+ transaction, American Express also added a new product, called V-Payment, to its product portfolio. V-Payment is unique in that it enables a tightly controlled, single-use card number for increased control.
</p><p>As of July 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, American Express offered several business, corporate and travel credit and charge cards and services and data and information services related to their use in the competitive markets for these cards.<sup id="cite_ref-DeLuna_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeLuna-70">[70]</a></sup></p><p>The online "American Express @ Work" function gives corporations a site on which to apply for, cancel or suspend cards, monitor policy compliance and track expenses. The cardholder company can create and generate reports for a corporate expense account program, including analytics and data consolidation or integration.<sup id="cite_ref-Kerr_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kerr-71">[71]</a></sup> Reports can be tailored for various sized companies. Through a Standard Expense Reporting feature in its "Manage Your Card Account site", American Express corporate cards provide cardholders access to pre-populated expense reports. The cardholder needs to annotate expenses and add out-of-pocket charges upon completion of which the report can be downloaded in electronic or paper format.<sup id="cite_ref-Kerr_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kerr-71">[71]</a></sup></p><p>American Express Corporate Card program can be used with a third-party on-demand expense management tool by Concur, a provider of integrated travel and expense management services.  This tool simplifies the creation of expense account reports and the corporate approval process. Corporate card activity, including viewing statements, making payments, setting up alerts and making inquiries and disputing charges, can be managed through an account online or via mobile device through this service.<sup id="cite_ref-Kerr_71-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kerr-71">[71]</a></sup></p><p>The corporate cards have benefits including discounts and rebates for travel and transportation, travel and emergency help, travel insurance and baggage protection.<sup id="cite_ref-Kerr_71-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kerr-71">[71]</a></sup> Upgrades from the Corporate "Green" Card to the Corporate Gold Card or Corporate Platinum Card, although subject to fees and terms and conditions, have several additional benefits at each card level, such as free breakfast or late checkout at many hotels.<sup id="cite_ref-Kerr_71-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kerr-71">[71]</a></sup> The American Express/Business Extra Corporate Credit Card is affiliated with American Airlines and provides a 4% rebate on eligible American Airlines travel purchased with the card.<sup id="cite_ref-Kerr_71-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kerr-71">[71]</a></sup></p><p>American Express has a specialized corporate meeting credit card.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Another specialized American Express business card is the American Express Corporate Purchasing Card, which can be assigned to individual employees or departments. Reconciliation and accounting services are available to make these functions easier for the corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-proprietary_cards">Non-proprietary cards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Non-proprietary cards" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In December 2000, American Express agreed to acquire the US$226<span class="nowrap"> </span>million credit card portfolio of <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Hawaii" title="Bank of Hawaii">Bank of Hawaii</a>, then a division of <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Century_Financial_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Century Financial Corporation">Pacific Century Financial Corp.</a><sup id="cite_ref-American-Express-Jan-2001-8-K_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American-Express-Jan-2001-8-K-74">[74]</a></sup> In January 2006, American Express sold its Bank of Hawaii card portfolio to <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America" title="Bank of America">Bank of America</a> (<a href="/wiki/MBNA" title="MBNA">MBNA</a>). Bank of America will issue <a href="/wiki/Visa_Inc." title="Visa Inc.">Visa</a> and American Express cards under the Bank of Hawaii name.
</p><p>Until 2004, Visa and <a href="/wiki/Mastercard" title="Mastercard">Mastercard</a> rules prohibited issuers of their cards from issuing American Express cards in the United States. This meant, as a practical matter, that U.S. banks could not issue American Express cards. These rules were struck-down as a result of antitrust litigation brought by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">U.S. Department of Justice</a>, and are no longer in effect.<sup id="cite_ref-American-Express-Mar-2004-10-K_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American-Express-Mar-2004-10-K-75">[75]</a></sup> In January 2004, American Express reached a deal to have its cards issued by a U.S. bank, <a href="/wiki/MBNA" title="MBNA">MBNA</a> America.<sup id="cite_ref-American-Express-Feb-2004-8-K_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American-Express-Feb-2004-8-K-76">[76]</a></sup> Initially decried by Mastercard executives as nothing but an "experiment", these cards were released in October 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-American-Express-Jan-2005-8-K_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American-Express-Jan-2005-8-K-77">[77]</a></sup> Some said that the relationship was going to be threatened by MBNA's merger with Bank of America, a major Visa issuer and original developer of Visa (and its predecessor, BankAmericard). However, an agreement was reached between American Express and Bank of America on December 21, 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-American-Express-Dec-2005-8-K_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American-Express-Dec-2005-8-K-78">[78]</a></sup> Under the terms of the agreement, Bank of America will own the customer loans and American Express will process the transactions. Also, American Express will dismiss Bank of America from its antitrust litigation against Visa, Mastercard, and a number of U.S. banks. Finally, both Bank of America and American Express also said an existing card-issuing partnership between MBNA and American Express will continue after the Bank of America-MBNA merger. The first card from the partnership, the no-annual-fee Bank of America Rewards American Express card, was released on June 30, 2006.
</p><p>Since then, <a href="/wiki/Citibank" title="Citibank">Citibank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo" title="Wells Fargo">Wells Fargo</a>, <a href="/wiki/First_National_Bank_of_Omaha" title="First National Bank of Omaha">First National Bank of Omaha</a>, <a href="/wiki/USAA" title="USAA">USAA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Synchrony_Financial" title="Synchrony Financial">Synchrony Financial</a>, and <a href="/wiki/US_Bancorp" class="mw-redirect" title="US Bancorp">US Bancorp</a> have started issuing American Express cards. Citi issues the <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy's">Macy's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bloomingdale%27s" title="Bloomingdale's">Bloomingdale's</a> American Express cards along with Citi-branded cards. Wells Fargo issues American Express cards under their own brand and for <a href="/wiki/Dillard%27s" title="Dillard's">Dillard's</a>. US Bancorp issues American Express-branded cards for US Bank along with Elan Card Services, a subsidiary that issues credit cards on behalf of small to midsize banks. Some <a href="/wiki/Credit_unions" class="mw-redirect" title="Credit unions">credit unions</a>, including <a href="/wiki/PenFed" class="mw-redirect" title="PenFed">PenFed</a>, also issue American Express cards. <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase" title="JPMorgan Chase">JPMorgan Chase</a> is the largest bank and the only <a href="/wiki/Big_Four_(banking)#United_States" title="Big Four (banking)">Big Four bank</a> in the US that does not partner with American Express. Instead, JPMorgan made the decision in 2013, to partner with Visa on the ChaseNet closed-loop network that is similar in terms of functionality to the American Express network.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Merchant_account">Merchant account</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Merchant account" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Many <a href="/wiki/Retail" title="Retail">retailers</a> do not accept American Express cards.<sup id="cite_ref-Digital_journal_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Digital_journal-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="how many? (October 2017)">specify</span></a></i>]</sup> American Express charges <a href="/wiki/Merchant_account" title="Merchant account">merchants</a> significantly higher fees than other credit card providers.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Motley_Fool_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Motley_Fool-80">[80]</a></sup>  In a court case <a href="/wiki/Ohio_v._American_Express_Co." title="Ohio v. American Express Co.">Ohio v. American Express Co.</a>, merchants filed a <a href="/wiki/Class_action" title="Class action">class action</a> lawsuit against American Express and claimed that charging high fees is a violation of the <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Antitrust_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Sherman Antitrust Act">Sherman Antitrust Act</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Law_360_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_360-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Buffalo_Law_Journal_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buffalo_Law_Journal-82">[82]</a></sup> According to the lawsuit, accepting American Express cards costs merchants the most.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-83">[83]</a></sup> In January 2017, the 2nd U.S. Circuit Court of Appeals affirmed a lower court ruling that American Express could block merchants that accept its cards from steering customers to other cards, like those offered by Visa and Mastercard.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> In June 2018, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">U.S. Supreme Court</a> affirmed the 2nd Circuit Court's ruling.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-card_products">Non-card products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Non-card products" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Traveler.27s_checks"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Traveler's_checks">Traveler's checks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Traveler's checks" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>American Express is the largest provider of <a href="/wiki/Traveler%27s_check" class="mw-redirect" title="Traveler's check">traveler's checks</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p><p>In 2005, American Express released the American Express Travelers Check Card, a <a href="/wiki/Stored-value_card" title="Stored-value card">stored-value card</a> that serves the same purposes as a traveler's check, but can be used in stores like a credit card. AmEx discontinued the card in October 2007, due to "changing market conditions" and issued refund checks to cardholders for the remaining balances.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Shearson.2FAmerican_Express"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Shearson/American_Express">Shearson/American Express</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Shearson/American Express" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Shearson/American_Express" class="mw-redirect" title="Shearson/American Express">Shearson/American Express</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shearson_AmEx_Logo.png" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0a/Shearson_AmEx_Logo.png/320px-Shearson_AmEx_Logo.png" decoding="async" width="320" height="47" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="821" data-file-height="121"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 320px;height: 47px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0a/Shearson_AmEx_Logo.png/320px-Shearson_AmEx_Logo.png" data-alt="" data-width="320" data-height="47" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shearson_AmEx_Logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Shearson/American Express logo c. 1982</div></div></div>
<p>During the 1980s, American Express began purchasing <a href="/wiki/Brokerage_firm" class="mw-redirect" title="Brokerage firm">stock brokerage</a> firms as part of an expansion. In mid-1981, it purchased <a href="/wiki/Sanford_I._Weill" title="Sanford I. Weill">Sanford I. Weill</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Shearson_Loeb_Rhoades" class="mw-redirect" title="Shearson Loeb Rhoades">Shearson Loeb Rhoades</a>, the second largest securities firm in the United States to form Shearson/American Express. Shearson Loeb Rhoades, itself was the culmination of several mergers in the 1970s as Weill's <a href="/wiki/Hayden,_Stone_%26_Co." title="Hayden, Stone &amp; Co.">Hayden, Stone &amp; Co.</a> merged with <a href="/wiki/Shearson,_Hammill_%26_Co." title="Shearson, Hammill &amp; Co.">Shearson, Hammill &amp; Co.</a> in 1974, to form <a href="/wiki/Shearson_Hayden_Stone" class="mw-redirect" title="Shearson Hayden Stone">Shearson Hayden Stone</a>. Shearson Hayden Stone then merged with <a href="/wiki/Loeb,_Rhoades,_Hornblower_%26_Co." class="mw-redirect" title="Loeb, Rhoades, Hornblower &amp; Co.">Loeb, Rhoades, Hornblower &amp; Co.</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Loeb,_Rhoades_%26_Co." title="Loeb, Rhoades &amp; Co.">Loeb, Rhoades &amp; Co.</a>) to form Shearson Loeb Rhoades in 1979. With capital totalling $250 million at the time of its acquisition, Shearson Loeb Rhoades trailed only <a href="/wiki/Merrill_Lynch" class="mw-redirect" title="Merrill Lynch">Merrill Lynch</a> as the securities industry's largest <a href="/wiki/Brokerage_firm" class="mw-redirect" title="Brokerage firm">brokerage firm</a>. After its acquisition by American Express, the firm was renamed Shearson/American Express.
</p><p>In 1984, Shearson/American Express purchased the 90-year-old <a href="/wiki/Investors_Diversified_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="Investors Diversified Services">Investors Diversified Services</a>, bringing with it a fleet of financial advisors and investment products. Also in 1984, American Express acquired the <a href="/wiki/Investment_banking" title="Investment banking">investment banking</a> and trading firm, <a href="/wiki/Lehman_Brothers" title="Lehman Brothers">Lehman Brothers Kuhn Loeb</a>, and added it to the Shearson family, creating Shearson Lehman/American Express. In 1988, the firm acquired <a href="/wiki/E._F._Hutton_%26_Co." class="mw-redirect" title="E. F. Hutton &amp; Co.">E. F. Hutton &amp; Co.</a>, forming <a href="/wiki/Shearson_Lehman_Hutton" class="mw-redirect" title="Shearson Lehman Hutton">Shearson Lehman Hutton</a> until 1990, when the firm's name became Shearson Lehman Brothers. When Harvey Golub took the reins in 1993, he negotiated the sale of Shearson's retail brokerage and <a href="/wiki/Investment_management" title="Investment management">asset management</a> business to <a href="/wiki/Primerica" title="Primerica">Primerica</a> and in following year, spun off of the remaining investment banking and institutional businesses as <a href="/wiki/Lehman_Brothers" title="Lehman Brothers">Lehman Brothers Holdings Inc</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_advisors">Financial advisors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Financial advisors" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On September 30, 2005, American Express spun-off its American Express Financial Advisors unit, <a href="/wiki/Ameriprise_Financial" title="Ameriprise Financial">Ameriprise Financial</a>, to its shareholders.  On September 30, 2005, <a href="/wiki/RSM_McGladrey" class="mw-redirect" title="RSM McGladrey">RSM McGladrey</a> acquired American Express Tax &amp; Business Services (TBS).<sup id="cite_ref-American-Express-Oct-2005-8-K_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American-Express-Oct-2005-8-K-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="International_bank">International bank</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: International bank" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2008, <a href="/wiki/Standard_Chartered_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Chartered Bank">Standard Chartered Bank</a> acquired American Express Bank Ltd, the international banking subsidiary of American Express for US$823<span class="nowrap"> </span>million.<sup id="cite_ref-American-Express-Sep-2007-8-K_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American-Express-Sep-2007-8-K-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Travel">Travel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Travel" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.<br><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22American+Express%22">"American Express"</a> – <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22American+Express%22+-wikipedia">news</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22American+Express%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22American+Express%22+-wikipedia">books</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22American+Express%22">scholar</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22American+Express%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">September 2019</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table><p>American Express established a Travel Division in 1915, that tied together all earlier efforts at making travel easier, and soon established its first <a href="/wiki/Travel_agency" title="Travel agency">travel agencies</a>. In the 1930s, the Travel Division had grown widely. <a href="/wiki/Albert_K._Dawson" title="Albert K. Dawson">Albert K. Dawson</a> was instrumental in expanding business operations overseas, even investing in tourist relations with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, Dawson was a photographer and film correspondent with the German army.
</p><p>In March 2014, American Express announced that it signed an agreement to create a joint venture for business travel and spun off its corporate travel business as <a href="/wiki/American_Express_Global_Business_Travel" title="American Express Global Business Travel">American Express Global Business Travel</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Publishing">Publishing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Publishing" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The American Express Publishing Corporation published the <i><a href="/wiki/Travel_%2B_Leisure" title="Travel + Leisure">Travel + Leisure</a>,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Food_%26_Wine_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Food &amp; Wine (magazine)">Food &amp; Wine</a>,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Executive_Travel_magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive Travel magazine">Executive Travel</a></i>, <i>Black Ink</i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Departures_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Departures Magazine">Departures</a></i> magazines until October 1, 2013, when it sold those titles to <a href="/wiki/Time_Inc." title="Time Inc.">Time Inc.</a><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup>  It publishes <i>American Express Skyguide</i> and is based in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-American-Express-Feb-2012-10-K_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American-Express-Feb-2012-10-K-94">[94]</a></sup> As of February 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Time_Inc." title="Time Inc.">Time Inc.</a> is restructuring the portfolio of publications.<sup id="cite_ref-Time_Inc._Lays_Out_Restructuring_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time_Inc._Lays_Out_Restructuring-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Individual_banking">Individual banking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Individual banking" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.<br><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22American+Express%22">"American Express"</a> – <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22American+Express%22+-wikipedia">news</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22American+Express%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22American+Express%22+-wikipedia">books</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22American+Express%22">scholar</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22American+Express%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">September 2019</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table><p>American Express FSB (<a href="/wiki/Federal_savings_bank" title="Federal savings bank">federal savings bank</a>) is a <a href="/wiki/Direct_bank" title="Direct bank">direct bank</a> offering a standard <a href="/wiki/Savings_account" title="Savings account">savings account</a> to individuals.  Checking account services are not provided.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Advertising_campaigns">Advertising campaigns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Advertising campaigns" data-section="33" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Don.27t_Leave_Home_Without_Them"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Don't_Leave_Home_Without_Them">Don't Leave Home Without Them</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Don't Leave Home Without Them" data-section="34" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1975, <a href="/wiki/David_Ogilvy_(businessman)" title="David Ogilvy (businessman)">David Ogilvy</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ogilvy_%26_Mather" class="mw-redirect" title="Ogilvy &amp; Mather">Ogilvy &amp; Mather</a> developed the highly successful "Don't Leave Home Without Them" <a href="/wiki/Advertising_campaign" title="Advertising campaign">ad campaign</a> for American Express Traveler's Cheques, featuring Oscar-award-winning actor <a href="/wiki/Karl_Malden" title="Karl Malden">Karl Malden</a>. Malden served as the public face of American Express Travelers Cheques for 25 years. In the UK, the spokesman was the <a href="/wiki/Celebrity" title="Celebrity">television personality</a> <a href="/wiki/Alan_Whicker" title="Alan Whicker">Alan Whicker</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p><p>After Malden's departure, and as the card assumed importance over the traveler's cheques, American Express continued to use celebrities, such as <a href="/wiki/Mel_Blanc" title="Mel Blanc">Mel Blanc</a> and ballerina <a href="/wiki/Cynthia_Gregory" title="Cynthia Gregory">Cynthia Gregory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> A typical ad for the American Express Card began with a celebrity asking viewers: "Do you know me?" Although he/she gave hints to his/her identity, the star's name was never mentioned except as imprinted on an American Express Card, after which announcer <a href="/wiki/Peter_Thomas_(television_narrator)" class="mw-redirect" title="Peter Thomas (television narrator)">Peter Thomas</a> told viewers how to apply for it.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Each ad concluded with the celebrity reminding viewers: "Don't Leave Home Without It." The "Don't Leave Home Without It" slogan was revived in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="The_Adventures_of_Seinfeld_.26_Superman"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Adventures_of_Seinfeld_&amp;_Superman">The Adventures of Seinfeld &amp; Superman</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: The Adventures of Seinfeld &amp; Superman" data-section="35" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seinfeld_superman.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7d/Seinfeld_superman.jpg/200px-Seinfeld_superman.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="121" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="181"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 121px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7d/Seinfeld_superman.jpg/200px-Seinfeld_superman.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="121" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Seinfeld_superman.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Seinfeld_%26_Superman" title="The Adventures of Seinfeld &amp; Superman">The Adventures of Seinfeld &amp; Superman</a></div></div></div>
<p>American Express continues to use celebrities in their ads. Some notable examples include a late 1990s ad campaign with comedian <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Seinfeld" title="Jerry Seinfeld">Jerry Seinfeld</a>, including the two 2004 <a href="/wiki/Webisode" title="Webisode">webisodes</a> in a series entitled "<a href="/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Seinfeld_%26_Superman" title="The Adventures of Seinfeld &amp; Superman">The Adventures of Seinfeld &amp; Superman</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="My_life._My_card._.2F_Are_You_a_Cardmember.3F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="My_life._My_card._/_Are_You_a_Cardmember?">My life. My card. / Are You a Cardmember?</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: My life. My card. / Are You a Cardmember?" data-section="36" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In late 2004, American Express launched the "My life. My card." brand campaign, and later the "Are You a Cardmember?" brand campaign in 2007, (both by Ogilvy &amp; Mather), featuring famous American Express cardmembers talking about their lives.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> The ads have featured actors/actresses <a href="/wiki/Kate_Winslet" title="Kate Winslet">Kate Winslet</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-amex-adsoftheworld-04/2009_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amex-adsoftheworld-04/2009-103">[103]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_De_Niro" title="Robert De Niro">Robert De Niro</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ken_Watanabe" title="Ken Watanabe">Ken Watanabe</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-amex-adsoftheworld-04/2009_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amex-adsoftheworld-04/2009-103">[103]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tina_Fey" title="Tina Fey">Tina Fey</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Duke_University" title="Duke University">Duke University</a> basketball coach <a href="/wiki/Mike_Krzyzewski" title="Mike Krzyzewski">Mike Krzyzewski</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> fashion designers <a href="/wiki/Collette_Dinnigan" title="Collette Dinnigan">Collette Dinnigan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diane_von_F%C3%BCrstenberg" title="Diane von Fürstenberg">Diane von Fürstenberg</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> comedian and talk show hostess <a href="/wiki/Ellen_DeGeneres" title="Ellen DeGeneres">Ellen DeGeneres</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> golfer <a href="/wiki/Tiger_Woods" title="Tiger Woods">Tiger Woods</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> professional snowboarder <a href="/wiki/Shaun_White" title="Shaun White">Shaun White</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> tennis pros <a href="/wiki/Venus_Williams" title="Venus Williams">Venus Williams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andy_Roddick" title="Andy Roddick">Andy Roddick</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Andre_Agassi" title="Andre Agassi">Andre Agassi</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MembersProjectAd_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MembersProjectAd-114">[114]</a></sup> surfer <a href="/wiki/Laird_Hamilton" title="Laird Hamilton">Laird Hamilton</a><sup id="cite_ref-amex-adsoftheworld-04/2009_103-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amex-adsoftheworld-04/2009-103">[103]</a></sup> Manchester United manager <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mourinho" title="José Mourinho">José Mourinho</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> film directors <a href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese" title="Martin Scorsese">Martin Scorsese</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-116"
