href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/M._Night_Shyamalan" title="M. Night Shyamalan">M. Night Shyamalan</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> singers <a href="/wiki/Sheryl_Crow" title="Sheryl Crow">Sheryl Crow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Keys" title="Alicia Keys">Alicia Keys</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MembersProjectAd_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MembersProjectAd-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Animals">Animals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Animals" data-section="37" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In 2007, a two-minute black-and-white ad, entitled "Animals" and starring <a href="/wiki/Ellen_DeGeneres" title="Ellen DeGeneres">Ellen DeGeneres</a>, won the <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Award</a> for Outstanding Commercial.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="C_F._Frost">C F. Frost</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: C F. Frost" data-section="38" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Many American Express credit card ads feature a sample American Express Card with the name "C. F. Frost" on the front. This is not a fabricated name; Charles F. Frost was an advertising executive at Ogilvy &amp; Mather.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Cause_marketing">Cause marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Cause marketing" data-section="39" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>American Express was one of the earliest users of <a href="/wiki/Cause_marketing" title="Cause marketing">cause marketing</a>, to great success.<sup id="cite_ref-forbescause_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbescause-123">[123]</a></sup> A 1983 promotion advertised that for each purchase made with an American Express Card, American Express would contribute one penny to the renovation of the <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Liberty" title="Statue of Liberty">Statue of Liberty</a>. The campaign generated contributions of $1.7 million to the Statue of Liberty restoration project. What would soon capture the attention of marketing departments of major corporations was that the promotion generated approximately a 28% increase in American Express card usage by consumers.
</p><p>In May 2007, American Express launched an initiative called the Members Project.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-American_Express_Rewards_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American_Express_Rewards-125">[125]</a></sup> Cardholders were invited to submit ideas for projects, and were told American Express was funding the winning project.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_projects">Cultural projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Cultural projects" data-section="40" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<p>American Express supports initiatives to enhance the architectural and cultural heritage, with the aim of raising awareness on the importance of historical and environmental conservation, through the restoration of historical monuments. American Express is a founder sponsor of the global program "World Monuments Watch",  launched in 1995, by <a href="/wiki/World_Monuments_Fund" title="World Monuments Fund">World Monuments Fund</a>. During the first edition of <a href="/wiki/Corporate_Art_Awards" title="Corporate Art Awards">Corporate Art Awards</a>, in 2016, American Express received by <a href="/wiki/PptArt" class="mw-redirect" title="PptArt">pptArt</a> the Corporate Art Award for its international restoration program.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Workplace">Workplace</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Workplace" data-section="41" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Offices">Offices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Offices" data-section="42" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:American_Express_Tower_9-11.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/American_Express_Tower_9-11.jpg/150px-American_Express_Tower_9-11.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="102" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4058" data-file-height="2764"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 150px;height: 102px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/American_Express_Tower_9-11.jpg/150px-American_Express_Tower_9-11.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="150" data-height="102" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:American_Express_Tower_9-11.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two <a href="/wiki/Rescue_and_recovery_effort_after_the_September_11_attacks" class="mw-redirect" title="Rescue and recovery effort after the September 11 attacks">rescue workers</a> entering the American Express Tower following <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11</a> terrorist attack on <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_(1973-2001)" class="mw-redirect" title="World Trade Center (1973-2001)">World Trade Center</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amex_House,_Edward_Street,_Brighton_(from_southeast).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Amex_House%2C_Edward_Street%2C_Brighton_%28from_southeast%29.jpg/150px-Amex_House%2C_Edward_Street%2C_Brighton_%28from_southeast%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="113" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1800"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 150px;height: 113px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Amex_House%2C_Edward_Street%2C_Brighton_%28from_southeast%29.jpg/150px-Amex_House%2C_Edward_Street%2C_Brighton_%28from_southeast%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="150" data-height="113" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amex_House,_Edward_Street,_Brighton_(from_southeast).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Amex_House" title="Amex House">Amex House</a> in <a href="/wiki/Brighton" title="Brighton">Brighton</a>, England, was built in 1977.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AmEx_Rome_2.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/AmEx_Rome_2.jpg/150px-AmEx_Rome_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="92" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="708" data-file-height="433"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 150px;height: 92px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/AmEx_Rome_2.jpg/150px-AmEx_Rome_2.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="150" data-height="92" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AmEx_Rome_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>American Express <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> HQ in Rome</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AmExSouthFlorida.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/AmExSouthFlorida.jpg/220px-AmExSouthFlorida.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4056" data-file-height="3040"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/AmExSouthFlorida.jpg/220px-AmExSouthFlorida.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AmExSouthFlorida.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An American Express regional HQ in Sunrise, Florida.</div></div></div>
<p>In April 1986, American Express moved its headquarters to the 51-story <a href="/wiki/Three_World_Financial_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Three World Financial Center">Three World Financial Center</a> in New York City. After <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">the events of September 11, 2001</a>, American Express had to leave its headquarters temporarily because it was located directly opposite the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_(1973-2001)" class="mw-redirect" title="World Trade Center (1973-2001)">World Trade Center</a> and was damaged during the fall of the towers. The company began gradually moving back into its rehabilitated building in 2002.
</p><p>The company maintains major offices in <a href="/wiki/Sunrise,_Florida" title="Sunrise, Florida">Sunrise, Florida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City" title="Salt Lake City">Salt Lake City</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>, with its main <a href="/wiki/Data_center" title="Data center">data centers</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> and Phoenix.
</p><p>AMEX Bank of Canada was founded in 1853, in Toronto. It currently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2019)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> has 3,000 employees in its head office at Sheppard, east of Highway 404 in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a> (relocated from <a href="/wiki/Markham,_Ontario" title="Markham, Ontario">Markham, Ontario</a>, a northern suburb of Toronto where it resided from 1985 to 2015), as well as an office in <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Hamilton, Ontario">Hamilton, Ontario</a>. The company began operations as a bank on July 1, 1990, following an <a href="/wiki/Order-in-council" class="mw-redirect" title="Order-in-council">order-in-council</a> made by the <a href="/wiki/Brian_Mulroney" title="Brian Mulroney">Brian Mulroney</a> government on November 21, 1988. This decision was not without controversy as federal banking policy at the time would not ordinarily have permitted American Express to operate as a bank.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup>  It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Bankers_Association" title="Canadian Bankers Association">Canadian Bankers Association</a> (CBA) and a registered member of the <a href="/wiki/Canada_Deposit_Insurance_Corporation" title="Canada Deposit Insurance Corporation">Canada Deposit Insurance Corporation</a> (CDIC), the federal agency insuring deposits at all of Canada's chartered banks.
</p><p>American Express has several offices in the UK, including a European Service Center in the <a href="/wiki/Carlton_Hill,_Brighton" title="Carlton Hill, Brighton">Carlton Hill</a> area of <a href="/wiki/Brighton" title="Brighton">Brighton</a>, England. The building was completed in 2012. It replaced American Express's former building, Amex House, a large white tower block built in 1977 and surrounded by several other smaller offices around the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Collis9_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collis9-128">[128]</a></sup>  The American Express European Service Center deals with card servicing, sales, fraud and merchant servicing. The official Europe, Middle East, and Africa HQ is located in the <a href="/wiki/Belgravia" title="Belgravia">Belgravia</a> district of Westminster, in <a href="/wiki/Central_London" title="Central London">central London</a>, at Belgrave House on Buckingham Palace Road, SW1; other UK offices are based in <a href="/wiki/Sussex" title="Sussex">Sussex</a> at <a href="/wiki/Burgess_Hill" title="Burgess Hill">Burgess Hill</a>. In November 2009, <a href="/wiki/Brighton_and_Hove" title="Brighton and Hove">Brighton and Hove</a> City Council granted planning permission for American Express to redevelop the Amex House site.
</p><p>The Japan, Asia-Pacific, and Australian Headquarters is co-located in Singapore, at <a href="/wiki/Collyer_Quay" title="Collyer Quay">16 Collyer Quay</a>, and in <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>'s <a href="/wiki/King_Street_Wharf" title="King Street Wharf">King Street Wharf</a> area.
</p><p>The headquarters of the Latin America and <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> division is in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale,_Florida" title="Fort Lauderdale, Florida">Fort Lauderdale, Florida</a>.
</p><p>American Express also has a significant presence in India. Its two centres are located at <a href="/wiki/Gurgaon" title="Gurgaon">Gurgaon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haryana" title="Haryana">Haryana</a> and on Mathura Road in <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi" title="New Delhi">New Delhi</a>. The Indian operations of American Express revolves around the <a href="/wiki/Back_office" title="Back office">back office</a> customer services operations apart from the credit card business for the domestic Indian Economy, arguably the American Express campus in Gurgaon is the largest employee location by head count for Amex and supports business continuity objectives of Amex including during Hurricane Sandy, the center works 24/7 and includes a co-located second building which was recently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (September 2019)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> transferred to a third party service provider but does much work for Amex.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Job_satisfaction">Job satisfaction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Job satisfaction" data-section="43" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2008, American Express was named the 62nd best company to work for in the United States by <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a></i>, ranking it number one for bank card companies.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> In October 2008, Amex Canada Inc. was named one of <a href="/wiki/Greater_Toronto%27s_Top_Employers" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Toronto's Top Employers">Greater Toronto's Top Employers</a> by Mediacorp Canada Inc., which was announced by the <i><a href="/wiki/Toronto_Star" title="Toronto Star">Toronto Star</a></i> newspaper.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> In 2018, <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a></i> ranked it the 23rd best company to work for.<sup id="cite_ref-fortune100best_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortune100best-131">[131]</a></sup> In 2019, <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a></i> ranked it the 9th best company to work for.<sup id="cite_ref-fortune100best_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortune100best-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Management_and_corporate_governance">Management and corporate governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Management and corporate governance" data-section="44" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
<p>The officers of the company are listed on the company's website as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-officersanddirectors_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officersanddirectors-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li>Stephen J. Squeri: chairman and chief executive officer</li>
<li>Douglas E. Buckminster: group president, global consumer services</li>
<li>Jeffrey C. Campbell: executive vice president and <a href="/wiki/Chief_financial_officer" title="Chief financial officer">chief financial officer</a></li>
<li>L. Kevin Cox: chief human resources officer</li>
<li>Paul D. Fabara: president, Global Services Group</li>
<li>Marc D. Gordon: executive vice president and chief information officer</li>
<li>Michael J. O'Neill: executive vice president, corporate affairs and communications</li>
<li>Denise Pickett: president, global risk, banking and compliance and chief risk officer</li>
<li>Elizabeth Rutledge: executive vice president and <a href="/wiki/Chief_marketing_officer" title="Chief marketing officer">chief marketing officer</a></li>
<li>Laureen E. Seeger: executive vice president and <a href="/wiki/General_counsel" title="General counsel">general counsel</a></li>
<li>Anré Williams: group president, global merchant and network services</li></ul><p>The members of the company's board of directors are listed on the company's website as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-officersanddirectors_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officersanddirectors-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li>Stephen J. Squeri: chairman and CEO of American Express Company</li>
<li>Charlene Barshefsky: senior international partner at WilmerHale</li>
<li>John J. Brennan: chairman emeritus and senior advisor of The Vanguard Group</li>
<li>Ursula Burns: chairman, VEON supervisory board</li>
<li>Peter Chernin: founder and CEO of The Chernin Group, LLC</li>
<li>Ralph de la Vega: chairman and founder of the De La Vega Group</li>
<li>Anne L. Lauvergeon: founder and CEO of A.L.P.</li>
<li>Michael O. Leavitt: founder, Leavitt Partners, LLC</li>
<li>Theodore J. Leonsis: chairman and CEO, Monumental Sports &amp; Entertainment, LLC</li>
<li>Richard C. Levin: senior advisor and former CEO, Coursera</li>
<li>Samuel J. Palmisano: former chairman, president and CEO, IBM</li>
<li>Daniel L. Vasella: honorary chairman and former chairman and CEO, Novartis AG</li>
<li>Robert D. Walter: founder and former chairman and chief executive officer, Cardinal Health, Inc.</li>
<li>Ronald A. Williams: former chairman and CEO of Aetna, Inc.</li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(10)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership">Ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Ownership" data-section="45" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-10 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-10">
<p>As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=American_Express&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, American Express shares are mainly held by institutional investors (<a href="/wiki/Berkshire_Hathaway" title="Berkshire Hathaway">Berkshire Hathaway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vanguard_group" class="mw-redirect" title="Vanguard group">Vanguard group</a>, <a href="/wiki/BlackRock" title="BlackRock">BlackRock</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_Street_Corporation" title="State Street Corporation">State Street Corporation</a> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup>)
</p>
